Ghazali's Demand for Proof: Composition's Impossibility
Ghazali demands proof for the impossibility of composition in God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's first objection against the philosophers: demanding proof for their claim that composition is impossible for God.

Core Idea
Before rejecting composition, one must prove its impossibility.

Ghazali launches his critique by focusing not on whether composition is possible, but on whether the philosophers have given any evidence for their claim. He points out that they have simply asserted that composition leads to a composite being and assumed this cannot apply to God. This lesson examines Ghazali's opening move: the demand for proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the structure of Ghazali's objection.
2
Identify the two aspects
Notice that Ghazali says his discussion has two aspects: a demand for proof and a refutation. This lesson covers the first.
The second aspect will be in the next lesson.
3
Understand the philosophers' argument
Ghazali summarizes the philosophers' reasoning: the second effect shares something with the First and differs, so it would be composite, which is impossible. He then challenges that.
He does not accept the impossibility without proof.
4
Grasp the challenge
Ghazali's key question: 'From where do you know the impossibility of this type of composition?' He demands evidence.
This is a methodological critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكلام عليه من وجهين مطالبة وإبطال . أما المطالبة فهى أن يقال : هذا حكاية المذهب ، فبم عرفتم استحالة ذلك في حق الأول ؟ ! حتى بنيتم عليه فى الاثينية ، إذ قلتم : إن الثاني ينبغي أن يشاركه فى شىء ويباينه فى شىء ، والذي فيه ما يشارك به ، وما يباين به ، فهو مركب ، والمركب محال . فنقول : هذا النوع من التركيب من أين عرفتم استحالته ولا دليل عليه
And the discussion of it is from two aspects: a demand for proof and a refutation. As for the demand, it is that one says: This is a narration of the doctrine. So by what do you know the impossibility of that with respect to the First? — such that you built upon it in the [issue of] duality, when you said: The second [effect] ought to share with Him in something and differ from Him in something, and that which has something by which it shares and something by which it differs is composite, and the composite is impossible. So we say: This type of composition — from where do you know its impossibility, while there is no proof for it?
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of Ghazali's critique of the philosophers' argument. He states that his discussion has two aspects: a demand for proof (muṭālabah) and a refutation (ibṭāl). Here he presents the first aspect. Ghazali says: you have narrated the doctrine (i.e., the philosophers' own position). Now, by what evidence do you know that the type of composition implied by sharing a genus is impossible for the First? Because you have built upon this impossibility a further claim about duality (al-ithnīniyyah?), namely that the second effect (the first intellect) must share with the First in something and differ in something, and that which has both sharing and differentiating attributes is composite, and the composite is impossible. Ghazali then directly challenges them: this type of composition — from where do you know its impossibility, and you have no proof for it? This is a pointed objection, implying that the philosophers have assumed without proof that such composition cannot apply to God. The passage ends with this challenge, setting up the next part of the critique.

Key Terms
مطالبة
إبطال
استحالة
تركيب
الاثينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ghazali rejects composition outright.
Correction: Here Ghazali does not assert that composition is possible or impossible; he only demands proof for the impossibility claim.

Checkpoint
What is the first aspect of Ghazali's critique against the philosophers?
A) A refutation of their argument
B) A demand for proof that composition is impossible for the First
C) A presentation of an alternative definition of God
D) A proof that God is composite

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's first objection is a methodological demand: philosophers must provide proof for their claim that composition is impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you affirm that Allah is one and incomparable, have you ever stopped to ask for proof that composition is impossible for Him? Where is your evidence?
?
The philosophers assumed the impossibility of composition without proof. What beliefs do you hold about Allah that you have accepted without verifying their proof?
?
Ghazali's demand challenges you: Do you have a proof for every claim you make about Allah's nature? If not, will you commit today to seeking proof from revelation and reason?

Ghazali's Demand: Proof for the Impossibility of Genus-Species Composition
Ghazali demands proof that composition from genus and species is impossible for the Necessary Existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's critique of the philosophers' claim that the First cannot be composite, and his argument that their proof only demonstrates a necessary being, not its simplicity.

Core Idea
The philosophers' proof only shows a stopping point, not a simple God.

In this lesson, we examine Ghazali's first criticism against the philosophers' doctrine that the First cannot have genus-species composition. He challenges them to provide a proof and then shows that their only argument is their own reasoning against divine attributes, which he has already refuted. Ghazali emphasizes that the rational proof only establishes a necessary being to halt infinite regress, not the specific attributes they claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Ghazali structures his argument: a demand followed by a refutation.
2
Identify the demand
Find where Ghazali asks the philosophers: 'By what do you know the impossibility of composition in the First?' This is the core of the first criticism.
The demand is introduced with 'As for the demand...'
3
Understand the philosophers' argument
The philosophers claim that if the First had genus and species, it would be composite and hence impossible. Their proof is based on the negation of attributes.
They argue that a composite from genus and species is either independent parts or dependent, both leading to impossibility.
4
Recognize Ghazali's refutation
Ghazali responds that he has already refuted this in his discussion on attributes. He states that the proof only indicates a cessation of causal chains, not additional attributes.
He says: 'the proof only indicated the cessation of the chain.'
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider that if the philosophers' definition of the Necessary Existent includes simplicity and no multiplicity, then even their own proof fails to establish such a being—it only shows a stopping point.
This undermines their entire construction of the second intellect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكلام عليه من وجهين مطالبة وإبطال . أما المطالبة فهى أن يقال : هذا حكاية المذهب ، فبم عرفتم استحالة ذلك في حق الأول ؟ ! حتى بنيتم عليه فى الاثينية ، إذ قلتم : إن الثاني ينبغي أن يشاركه فى شىء ويباينه فى شىء ، والذي فيه ما يشارك به ، وما يباين به ، فهو مركب ، والمركب محال . فنقول : هذا النوع من التركيب من أين عرفتم استحالته ولا دليل عليه إلا قولكم المحكى عنكم فى نفي الصفات ، وهو أن المركب من الجنس والفصل ، مجتمع من أجزاء، فإن كان يصح لواحد : من الأجزاء ، أو الجملة، في حال، وجود دون الآخر ؛ فهو واجب الوجود دون ما عداه ؛ وإن كان لا للأجزاء ، وجود ، دون المجتمع ، ولا للمجتمع وجود دون الأجزاء ، فالكل معلول محتاج . وقد تكلمنا عليه فى الصفات . وبينا أن ذلك ليس بمحال ، في قطع تسلسل العلل ، والبرهان لم يدل إلا على قطع التسلسل . فأما العظائم التي اخترعتموها في لزوم اتصاف واجب الوجود بها ، فلم يدل عليها دليل ؛ فإن كان واجب الوجود ، ما وصفوه به ، وهو أنه لا يكون فيه كثرة ، فلا يحتاج في قوامه إلى غيره ، فلا دليل إذن على إثبات واجب الوجود ؛ وإنما الدليل دل على قطع التسلسل فقط ، وهذا قد فرغنا منه في الصفات وهو في هذا النوع أظهر
And the discussion about it is from two aspects: a demand and a refutation. As for the demand, it is that it is said: This is a narration of the doctrine; by what do you know the impossibility of that in respect of the First? Until you built upon it in the [doctrine of] second [intellect]? For you said: The second should share something with it and differ in something, and that which has something by which it shares and something by which it differs is composite, and the composite is impossible. So we say: This type of composition, from where do you know its impossibility and there is no proof for it except your statement related from you in the negation of attributes—namely that the composite from genus and species is assembled from parts; if it is valid for one of the parts or the whole, in a state, to exist without the other, then it is necessary of existence without what is other than it; and if there is no existence for the parts without the composite, nor for the composite without the parts, then the whole is an effect, dependent. And we have spoken about this in [the discussion on] attributes. And we have shown that this is not impossible in the cessation of the chain of causes, and the proof only indicated the cessation of the chain. As for the great things you have invented in the necessity of the Necessary Existent being characterized by them, no proof indicated them; for if the Necessary Existent is what they described it to be—that there is no multiplicity in it, and it does not need in its constitution something else—then there is no proof for establishing the Necessary Existent; the proof only indicated the cessation of the chain, and nothing more. And this we have finished in [the discussion on] attributes, and it is even more evident in this type.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents the first of two criticisms Ghazali makes against the philosophers' doctrine that the First cannot have genus-species composition. He calls this criticism a 'demand' (mutalaba). Ghazali asks: On what basis do you claim that such composition is impossible for the First? You built upon it your doctrine of the second intellect, saying that the second must share and differ with the First, implying composition. Ghazali then says: The only proof you have is your own argument in the negation of attributes—that composition from genus and species implies parts, and if one part can exist without the other, that part would be necessary; if not, the whole is dependent. But Ghazali asserts that he has already refuted this argument in his discussion on divine attributes. He maintains that this type of composition is not impossible in the context of stopping the infinite regress of causes. The demonstrable proof only indicates a stopping point (a necessary being), but it does not prove the specific attributes you have invented, like the absence of any multiplicity. In fact, if the Necessary Existent is defined by you as having no multiplicity and needing nothing else, then the proof does not even prove the existence of such an entity—it only proves a cessation of the chain. So their argument is baseless.

Key Terms
مطالبة
إبطال
تركيب
جنس
فصل
واجب الوجود
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers have a solid proof that the First must be absolutely simple and cannot have any composition.
Correction: Ghazali argues that their proof only shows a necessary being to stop infinite regress, not that it lacks genus-species composition. Their argument is based on an unsubstantiated assumption and has been refuted in the discussion on attributes.

Checkpoint
What does Ghazali say about the philosophers' proof that the First cannot be composite?
A) It is valid and proven
B) It only proves cessation of causal chains, not the specific attributes
C) It is based on revelation
D) It is a logical necessity

Key Takeaway
Ghazali exposes that the philosophers' proof for the First's simplicity is insufficient; it only demonstrates a necessary being, not the absence of composition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you describe Allah as 'self-sufficient' or 'one', do you base that on revelation or on your own reasoning? This lesson shows that human proof alone cannot guarantee these attributes—what does that mean for how you approach learning about Allah's nature?
?
Ghazali accuses the philosophers of 'inventing great things' and attributing them to Allah without proof. Are you ever tempted to add your own requirements to what Allah must be like, beyond what is taught in the Qur'an and sunnah? Repent from that tendency right now.

The Meaning of 'Necessary of Existence' and the Impossibility of Two Creators
Ghazali presents the philosophers' dilemma and his terminological critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali argues that the term 'necessary of existence' is the source of confusion in the philosophers' argument against two distinct necessary existents.

Core Idea
The term 'necessary of existence' does not by itself prove uniqueness.

In this passage, Ghazali presents the philosophers' claim that two necessary existents are impossible because their distinctness would require a condition that either applies to both or is unnecessary. He then identifies the root of their error: the ambiguous term 'necessary of existence'. By replacing it with a clearer definition, he shows that the philosophers have no proof against multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' objection
Read the part of the passage where the philosophers argue that two distinct necessary existents are impossible because the differentiator would either be a condition for necessity (applying to both) or not (making necessity dependent on something else).
This is a classic dilemma: either condition applies to both or neither.
2
Notice Ghazali's diagnosis
Ghazali says this is the same confusion as with attributes, and the source is the term 'necessary of existence'. He suggests dropping it.
3
Understand the alternative definition
Ghazali proposes replacing 'necessary of existence' with 'existent without agent, eternal'. He then challenges the philosophers to prove that such an existent cannot be multiple.
This shifts the burden of proof back to the philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن أي وجه يستحيل هذا في العلل ؟ ! وبهذا يتبين عجزهم عن نفى إلهين صانعين فإن قيل : إنما يستحيل هذا ، من حيث إن ما به المباينة بين الذاتين ، إن كان شرطاً في وجوب الوجود ، فينبغى أن يوجد لكل واجب وجود ، فلا يتباينان ، وإن لم يكن هذا شرطاً ، ولا الآخر شرطاً ، فكل ما لا يشترط في وجوب الوجود ، فوجوده مستغنى عنه ، ويتم وجوب الوجود بغيره . قلنا : هذا عين ما ذكرتموه فى الصفات ، وقد تكلمنا عليه ، ومنشأ التلبيس ذلك ، في لفظ « واجب الوجود » ، فليطرح ; فإنا لا نسلم أن الدليل جميع يدل على « واجب الوجود » ، إن لم يكن المراد به « موجود لا فاعل له قديم » فإن كان المراد هذا ، فليترك واجب الوجود » ، وليبين : أن موجوداً لا علة له ولا فاعل ، يستحيل فيد التعدد والتباين ، ولا يقوم عليه دليل . فيبقى قولهم : إن ذلك هل هو شرط فى « أن لا تكون له علة » ، فهو هوس ، فإن ما لا علة له قد ببينا أنه لا يعلل كونه لا علة له ، حتى يطلب شرطه ; وهو كقول القائل : إن السوادية هل هى شرط فى كون اللون لوناً ؟ ! فإن كانت شرطاً ، فلم كانت الحمرة لوناً ؟ ! فيقال: أما في حقيقته فلا يشترط واحد منهما - أعنى ثبوت حقيقة اللونية فى العقل - ، وأما فى وجوده ، فالشرط أحدهما لا بعينه - أى لا يمكن جنس فى الوجود إلا وله فصل -
From which perspective is this impossible among causes?! By this their incapacity to deny two makers becomes clear. For if it is said: This is only impossible because that by which the two essences are distinguished, if it is a condition for the necessity of existence, then it should exist for every necessary existent, so they would not be distinct; and if it is not a condition, nor is the other a condition, then everything that is not a condition for the necessity of existence, its existence is dispensable, and the necessity of existence is completed by other than it. We say: This is exactly what you mentioned regarding attributes, and we have discussed it. The source of the confusion is the term 'necessary of existence', so let it be discarded; for we do not admit that the proof indicates a 'necessary of existence' unless by it is meant 'an existent that has no agent, eternal'. If this is meant, then leave 'necessary of existence' and make clear that an existent that has no cause and no agent is impossible to have multiplicity and distinction, and no proof establishes this. So their statement remains: 'Is that a condition for having no cause?' This is nonsense, for that which has no cause we have shown that its having no cause is not caused, such that its condition is sought. It is like the statement of the speaker: 'Is blackness a condition for being a color?' If it is a condition, then why is redness a color? It is said: As for its essence, neither is a condition – meaning the subsistence of the reality of color in the mind – but as for its existence in the external world, the condition is one of the two not specifically determined – i.e., no genus can exist in existence except with a differentia.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the philosophers' argument that two distinct necessary existents are impossible. Ghazali begins by rhetorically asking why it is impossible for causal chains to end in two distinct causes, then states that this exposes their inability to deny two creators. He then presents the philosophers' objection: the differentia that distinguishes two essences, if it is a condition for necessary existence, would apply to both and they would not be distinct; if not, then the differentia is unnecessary and necessity is from something else. Ghazali responds by noting this is the same confusion as with attributes, already addressed. The root of the confusion is the term 'necessary of existence'. He proposes replacing it with 'existent without agent, eternal', arguing that once this is done, the philosophers have no proof that such an existent cannot be multiple. Their remaining question about whether the differentia is a condition for having no cause is nonsense, because having no cause is not caused and thus has no condition. He draws an analogy: asking whether blackness is a condition for being a color is absurd because color's essence does not require any particular shade; in existence, any genus requires a differentia, but that does not entail the impossibility of multiple species under the same genus.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود
إلهين صانعين
المباينة
الشرط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'necessary of existence' itself implies that there can only be one such existent.
Correction: Ghazali shows that 'necessary of existence' is ambiguous and does not logically entail uniqueness. Only when defined as 'existent without agent' does the question of multiplicity arise, and even then the philosophers have no proof.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the source of confusion in the philosophers' argument against two necessary existents?
A) The concept of causality
B) The term 'necessary of existence'
C) The distinction between genus and species
D) The analogy of blackness and color

Key Takeaway
Ghazali argues that the philosophers' proof against two necessary existents fails because the term 'necessary of existence' is ambiguous and does not entail uniqueness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the oneness of Allah, do you rely on terms you don't fully understand? How does this lesson challenge you to examine the foundations of your belief? Commit to studying the proofs of tawhid with humility, not just repeating words.
?
Ghazali points out that the term 'necessary of existence' can be misleading. In your own understanding of Allah, are there any concepts or terms you use without critically examining their meaning? What is at stake if we get the terminology wrong? Resolve to clarify your understanding of each attribute of Allah.
?
The philosophers' proof seemed logical, but Ghazali exposed its flaw. How does this affect your trust in human reasoning about Allah? Are you willing to accept the limits of your own intellect before His majesty? Make a concrete plan to deepen your knowledge through authentic sources.

Why Conditions Cannot Apply to the Uncaused
Ghazali refutes the condition argument and uses an analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's refutation of the claim that distinctness is a condition for having no cause, and his analogy with blackness and color.

Core Idea
Something without a cause cannot have conditions for its uncausedness.

In this part, Ghazali addresses the philosophers' remaining question: is the distinctness a condition for having no cause? He dismisses it as nonsense, because having no cause is itself uncaused and therefore cannot have conditions. He illustrates this with an analogy: asking whether blackness is a condition for being a color is absurd because color's essence does not require any specific shade.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's dismissal
He calls the question 'nonsense' (هوس) because something that has no cause cannot have its causelessness conditioned.
2
Understand why it is nonsense
Ghazali explains that the uncaused is not caused, so it cannot have a condition. To seek a condition for uncausedness is like seeking a cause for what has no cause.
3
Analyze the analogy
The analogy: asking whether blackness is a condition for color is wrong because the essence of color does not require blackness. Similarly, uncausedness has no condition.
In existence, any color must have a specific hue, but that does not make the hue a condition for color itself. Similarly, distinctness may exist but is not a condition for uncausedness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن أي وجه يستحيل هذا في العلل ؟ ! وبهذا يتبين عجزهم عن نفى إلهين صانعين فإن قيل : إنما يستحيل هذا ، من حيث إن ما به المباينة بين الذاتين ، إن كان شرطاً في وجوب الوجود ، فينبغى أن يوجد لكل واجب وجود ، فلا يتباينان ، وإن لم يكن هذا شرطاً ، ولا الآخر شرطاً ، فكل ما لا يشترط في وجوب الوجود ، فوجوده مستغنى عنه ، ويتم وجوب الوجود بغيره . قلنا : هذا عين ما ذكرتموه فى الصفات ، وقد تكلمنا عليه ، ومنشأ التلبيس ذلك ، في لفظ « واجب الوجود » ، فليطرح ; فإنا لا نسلم أن الدليل جميع يدل على « واجب الوجود » ، إن لم يكن المراد به « موجود لا فاعل له قديم » فإن كان المراد هذا ، فليترك واجب الوجود » ، وليبين : أن موجوداً لا علة له ولا فاعل ، يستحيل فيد التعدد والتباين ، ولا يقوم عليه دليل . فيبقى قولهم : إن ذلك هل هو شرط فى « أن لا تكون له علة » ، فهو هوس ، فإن ما لا علة له قد ببينا أنه لا يعلل كونه لا علة له ، حتى يطلب شرطه ; وهو كقول القائل : إن السوادية هل هى شرط فى كون اللون لوناً ؟ ! فإن كانت شرطاً ، فلم كانت الحمرة لوناً ؟ ! فيقال: أما في حقيقته فلا يشترط واحد منهما - أعنى ثبوت حقيقة اللونية فى العقل - ، وأما فى وجوده ، فالشرط أحدهما لا بعينه - أى لا يمكن جنس فى الوجود إلا وله فصل -
From which perspective is this impossible among causes?! By this their incapacity to deny two makers becomes clear. For if it is said: This is only impossible because that by which the two essences are distinguished, if it is a condition for the necessity of existence, then it should exist for every necessary existent, so they would not be distinct; and if it is not a condition, nor is the other a condition, then everything that is not a condition for the necessity of existence, its existence is dispensable, and the necessity of existence is completed by other than it. We say: This is exactly what you mentioned regarding attributes, and we have discussed it. The source of the confusion is the term 'necessary of existence', so let it be discarded; for we do not admit that the proof indicates a 'necessary of existence' unless by it is meant 'an existent that has no agent, eternal'. If this is meant, then leave 'necessary of existence' and make clear that an existent that has no cause and no agent is impossible to have multiplicity and distinction, and no proof establishes this. So their statement remains: 'Is that a condition for having no cause?' This is nonsense, for that which has no cause we have shown that its having no cause is not caused, such that its condition is sought. It is like the statement of the speaker: 'Is blackness a condition for being a color?' If it is a condition, then why is redness a color? It is said: As for its essence, neither is a condition – meaning the subsistence of the reality of color in the mind – but as for its existence in the external world, the condition is one of the two not specifically determined – i.e., no genus can exist in existence except with a differentia.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the philosophers' argument that two distinct necessary existents are impossible. Ghazali begins by rhetorically asking why it is impossible for causal chains to end in two distinct causes, then states that this exposes their inability to deny two creators. He then presents the philosophers' objection: the differentia that distinguishes two essences, if it is a condition for necessary existence, would apply to both and they would not be distinct; if not, then the differentia is unnecessary and necessity is from something else. Ghazali responds by noting this is the same confusion as with attributes, already addressed. The root of the confusion is the term 'necessary of existence'. He proposes replacing it with 'existent without agent, eternal', arguing that once this is done, the philosophers have no proof that such an existent cannot be multiple. Their remaining question about whether the differentia is a condition for having no cause is nonsense, because having no cause is not caused and thus has no condition. He draws an analogy: asking whether blackness is a condition for being a color is absurd because color's essence does not require any particular shade; in existence, any genus requires a differentia, but that does not entail the impossibility of multiple species under the same genus.

Key Terms
العلة
الشرط
السوادية
اللون
الفصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Distinctness must be a condition for something to be uncaused, so two uncaused beings would require distinct conditions.
Correction: Ghazali shows that uncausedness has no conditions, so the question itself is invalid. The analogy with color demonstrates that the essence of color does not require a specific shade, just as uncausedness does not require a specific differentiator.

Checkpoint
Ghazali compares the question of whether distinctness is a condition for having no cause to which of the following?
A) Asking whether redness is a condition for blackness
B) Asking whether blackness is a condition for being a color
C) Asking whether a cause is needed for an effect
D) Asking whether a genus requires a differentia

Key Takeaway
Since having no cause is not caused, it cannot have a condition; therefore the question of whether distinctness is a condition for uncausedness is meaningless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there questions you ask about Allah—like 'Why is He this way?'—that assume He needs a condition for His attributes, even though He is uncaused? How will you train yourself to stop such thoughts?
?
When you feel doubts about your faith, do you ever realize those doubts might be based on flawed reasoning—demanding conditions for the Unconditioned? Will you commit to examining the logic behind your doubts before accepting them?
?
This lesson shows that some theological puzzles vanish when we distinguish essence from existence. In your own life, do you confuse what is essential to your identity with what is contingent? Reflect on one area where this distinction might free you from unnecessary anxiety.

Refuting the Condition for Distinction Between Two Necessarily Existent Beings
Ghazali criticizes the term 'wajib al-wujud' and refutes the condition argument using the color analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali discards the term 'wajib al-wujud' and how he refutes the philosophers' argument that a condition for distinction would preclude two necessary existents.

Core Idea
The term 'necessary existent' obscures the real issue; replace it with 'existent with no cause'.

Ghazali begins by exposing the confusion surrounding the term 'wajib al-wujud'. He argues that this term leads to ambiguity and instead proposes to focus on the concept of an existent without a cause. He then tackles the philosophers' argument that distinction between two such beings would require a condition, using an analogy from color to show its logical flaws.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's critique of the term
Read the passage where Ghazali points out that the confusion arises from the term 'wajib al-wujud' and suggests discarding it. Notice his emphasis on focusing on 'existent with no cause'.
This sets the stage for the subsequent argument.
2
Analyze the condition argument
Identify the philosophers' claim: the distinguishing factor between two necessary existents must either be a condition for necessary existence (making them identical) or not (making it dispensable). Ghazali calls this nonsense.
He argues that something with no cause does not have its no-causation caused, so no condition is needed.
3
Understand the color analogy
Examine how Ghazali uses the example of blackness and redness to illustrate that a condition for existence (outside the mind) can be one of two differentiae without being specifically determined. This shows the flaw in the philosophers' reasoning.
The analogy demonstrates that distinction is possible without a specific condition for each.
4
Connect to the larger argument
Reflect on how this refutation undermines the philosophers' claim that two gods are impossible. The passage ends with the positor of two causes using this logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن أي وجه يستحيل هذا في العلل؟! وبهذا يتبين عجزهم عن نفى إلهين صانعين.
فإن قيل: إنما يستحيل هذا من حيث إن ما به المباينة بين الذاتين، إن كان شرطاً في وجوب الوجود، فينبغى أن يوجد لكل واجب وجود، فلا يتباينان، وإن لم يكن هذا شرطاً، ولا الآخر شرطاً، فكل ما لا يشترط في وجوب الوجود، فوجوده مستغنى عنه، ويتم وجوب الوجود بغيره.
قلنا: هذا عين ما ذكرتموه في الصفات، وقد تكلمنا عليه، ومنشأ التلبيس ذلك، في لفظ «واجب الوجود»، فليطرح؛ فإنا لا نسلم أن الدليل جميع يدل على «واجب الوجود» إن لم يكن المراد به «موجود لا فاعل له قديم» فإن كان المراد هذا، فليترك واجب الوجود، وليبين: أن موجوداً لا علة له ولا فاعل، يستحيل فيه التعدد والتباين، ولا يقوم عليه دليل.
فيبقى قولهم: إن ذلك هل هو شرط في «أن لا تكون له علة»، فهو هوس، فإن ما لا علة له قد بينا أنه لا يعلل كونه لا علة له، حتى يطلب شرطه؛ وهو كقول القائل: إن السوادية هل هي شرط في كون اللون لوناً؟! فإن كانت شرطاً، فلم كانت الحمرة لوناً؟! فيقال: أما في حقيقته فلا يشترط واحد منهما - أعنى ثبوت حقيقة اللونية في العقل -، وأما في وجوده، فالشرط أحدهما لا بعينه - أى لا يمكن جنس في الوجود إلا وله فصل.
فكذلك من يثبت علتين ويقطع التسلسل بهما، فيقول: يتباينان بفصول، وأحد الفصول شرط الوجود، لا محالة، ولكن لا على التعيين: فإن قيل: هذا يجوز في اللون، فإن له وجوداً مضافاً إلى الماهية، زائداً على الماهية؛ ولا يجوز في واجب الوجود، إذ ليس له إلا وجوب الوجود، وليس ثمت ماهية يضاف الوجود إليها؛ وكما أن فصل السواد وفصل الحمرة، لا يشترط تلونية في كونها لونية، إنما يشترط في وجودها الحاصل بعلة، فكذلك ينبغى ألا يشترط في الوجود الواجب، فإن الوجود الواجب للأول كاللونية للون، لا كالوجود المضاف إلى اللونية.
قلنا: لا نسلم، بل إن له حقيقة موصوفة بالوجود، على ما سنبينه في المسألة التي بعد هذه، وقولهم: إنه وجود بلا ماهية خارج عن المعقول. ورجع حاصل الكلام إلى أنهم بنوا نفى التثنية على نفي التركيب الجنسي والفصلى، ثم بنوا ذلك على نفى الماهية وراء الوجود، فمهما أبطلنا الأخير، الذي هو أساس الأساس، بطل الكل عليهم، وهو بنيان ضعيف الثبوت، قريب من بيوت العنكبوت.
From what aspect is this impossible in causes? And by this their inability to deny two makers becomes clear. For it is said: This is only impossible because that by which there is distinction between the two essences, if it is a condition for the necessity of existence, then it should be found in every necessary existent, so they would not be distinct. And if this is not a condition, nor the other a condition, then everything that is not a condition for the necessity of existence, its existence is dispensable, and the necessity of existence is completed by something else. We said: This is exactly what you mentioned concerning the attributes, and we have spoken about it. The source of the confusion is in the term 'necessarily existent (wajib al-wujud)', so let it be discarded. For we do not concede that the proof indicates 'necessarily existent' if 'eternal existent with no agent' is not intended. If this is intended, then let 'necessarily existent' be left aside, and let it be shown that an existent with no cause and no agent, multiplicity and distinction are impossible in it, and no proof establishes it. So their statement remains: Is that [the distinguishing factor] a condition for 'that it have no cause'? It is nonsense. For that which has no cause, we have shown that its having no cause is not caused, so that its condition might be sought. It is like one saying: Is blackness a condition for color being color? If it were a condition, why is redness a color? So it is said: As for its essence (i.e., color-ness), neither of the two is a condition – I mean the subsistence of the reality of color-ness in the mind – and as for its existence (outside the mind), the condition is one of them not specifically determined – i.e., no genus can exist except with a differentia. Likewise, one who posits two causes and terminates the regress by them says: They are distinguished by differentiae, and one of the differentiae is a condition for existence necessarily, but not specifically determined. If it is said: This is permissible for color, for it has an existence added to the quiddity, additional to the quiddity; but it is not permissible for the necessarily existent, for it has only the necessity of existence, and there is no quiddity to which existence is added. And just as the differentia of blackness and the differentia of redness are not a condition for color-ness in its being color-ness, rather they are a condition for its existence that comes about by a cause, so likewise it should not be a condition for the necessary existence, for the necessary existence of the First is like color-ness for color, not like existence added to color-ness. We said: We do not concede. Rather, it has a reality qualified by existence, as we will clarify in the following question. And their statement that it is existence without quiddity is beyond the intelligible. The gist of the matter is that they built the denial of duality on the denial of generic and specific composition, and then built that on the denial of quiddity beyond existence. So once we invalidate the last, which is the foundation of foundations, everything becomes invalid for them, and it is a weak structure, near to spiders' webs.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument. Ghazali responds to the philosophers' claim that two gods are impossible because their distinguishing factor would either be a condition for necessary existence (leading to identical conditions) or not (making it dispensable). Ghazali first points out that the confusion stems from the term 'necessary existent' (wajib al-wujud); he suggests replacing it with 'existent with no cause' to avoid ambiguity. He then argues that the philosophers' question about whether the distinguishing factor is a condition for having no cause is nonsense, because having no cause is not caused and thus requires no condition. He illustrates this with the analogy of blackness and redness: neither is a condition for the essence of color-ness, but for existence, one of them is a condition (but not specifically determined). The philosophers object that this analogy fails because color has an existence added to quiddity, while the necessary existent has only its necessity. Ghazali responds by affirming that the First has a reality qualified by existence, promising to prove this later, and he dismisses the notion of existence without quiddity as unintelligible. He concludes that the philosophers' entire argument against duality rests on shaky foundations (denial of quiddity beyond existence), and once that is refuted, their case collapses like a spider's web.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود
شرط
مباينة
علة
فصل
جنس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers think the term 'wajib al-wujud' automatically implies uniqueness and that any distinction would require a condition that either makes them identical or unnecessary.
Correction: Ghazali shows that the term is ambiguous; the real concept ('existent with no cause') does not preclude multiplicity, and the condition argument fails because no-causation is not caused, so no condition is needed. The color analogy shows that distinction is possible without a specific condition.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the source of confusion in the philosophers' argument?
A) The concept of cause
B) The term 'wajib al-wujud'
C) The distinction between essence and existence
D) The nature of color

Key Takeaway
Ghazali refutes the philosophers' condition argument by showing that the term 'necessary existent' is misleading and that distinction between two uncaused beings is logically possible, as illustrated by the color analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the oneness of God, do you ever feel a tension between what your intellect demands and what revelation teaches? How does Ghazali's logical argument—that two uncaused beings are not impossible in principle—force you to confront the difference between rational necessity and revealed truth? What does that say about the limits of your own reasoning in matters of faith?
?
Consider the term 'necessary existent' as a label for God. Have you ever used philosophical language about God in a way that actually obscured His true nature? How might this lesson's insistence on precise terms (like 'existent with no cause') challenge you to be more careful in how you speak about Allah, especially when defending tawhid to others?
?
Ghazali's color analogy shows that in the mind, conditions are not predetermined, but in reality, they are. In your life, have you ever acted as if multiple 'ultimate authorities' (e.g., career, family, desires) could coexist without a single overarching condition? Where might you be living as if there is more than one 'uncaused' source of meaning, and how does this lesson call you to submit to the One who alone requires no cause?

The Objection of Quiddity and the Collapse of the Philosophers' Argument
Ghazali answers the philosophers' objection about quiddity and existence and declares their argument a weak structure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's response to the objection that the color analogy fails for the necessary existent, and why he considers the philosophers' entire argument a weak structure.

Core Idea
The philosophers' denial of quiddity beyond existence is unintelligible; their argument rests on a foundation of spiders' webs.

The philosophers counter that the color analogy does not apply to the necessary existent, as it has no quiddity separate from existence—only necessity. Ghazali responds by affirming that the First has a reality qualified by existence, and he dismisses the notion of existence without quiddity as irrational. He concludes that the entire argument against two gods is built on weak premises, namely the denial of quiddity beyond existence, which he promises to refute later.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' objection
The philosophers argue that the color analogy fails because color has existence added to quiddity, whereas the necessary existent is pure necessity without quiddity.
They claim that the condition for existence in the analogy applies only to contingent things.
2
Understand Ghazali's response
Ghazali rejects this, stating that the First has a reality qualified by existence, and the notion of existence without quiddity is unintelligible (outside the mind). He promises to prove this later.
He thus defends the applicability of the analogy.
3
See the conclusion
Ghazali summarizes that the philosophers' entire denial of duality is built on denying quiddity beyond existence. Once that foundation is invalidated, their whole argument collapses like a spider's web.
This is a strong rhetorical finish, showing the weakness of their position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن أي وجه يستحيل هذا في العلل؟! وبهذا يتبين عجزهم عن نفى إلهين صانعين.
فإن قيل: إنما يستحيل هذا من حيث إن ما به المباينة بين الذاتين، إن كان شرطاً في وجوب الوجود، فينبغى أن يوجد لكل واجب وجود، فلا يتباينان، وإن لم يكن هذا شرطاً، ولا الآخر شرطاً، فكل ما لا يشترط في وجوب الوجود، فوجوده مستغنى عنه، ويتم وجوب الوجود بغيره.
قلنا: هذا عين ما ذكرتموه في الصفات، وقد تكلمنا عليه، ومنشأ التلبيس ذلك، في لفظ «واجب الوجود»، فليطرح؛ فإنا لا نسلم أن الدليل جميع يدل على «واجب الوجود» إن لم يكن المراد به «موجود لا فاعل له قديم» فإن كان المراد هذا، فليترك واجب الوجود، وليبين: أن موجوداً لا علة له ولا فاعل، يستحيل فيه التعدد والتباين، ولا يقوم عليه دليل.
فيبقى قولهم: إن ذلك هل هو شرط في «أن لا تكون له علة»، فهو هوس، فإن ما لا علة له قد بينا أنه لا يعلل كونه لا علة له، حتى يطلب شرطه؛ وهو كقول القائل: إن السوادية هل هي شرط في كون اللون لوناً؟! فإن كانت شرطاً، فلم كانت الحمرة لوناً؟! فيقال: أما في حقيقته فلا يشترط واحد منهما - أعنى ثبوت حقيقة اللونية في العقل -، وأما في وجوده، فالشرط أحدهما لا بعينه - أى لا يمكن جنس في الوجود إلا وله فصل.
فكذلك من يثبت علتين ويقطع التسلسل بهما، فيقول: يتباينان بفصول، وأحد الفصول شرط الوجود، لا محالة، ولكن لا على التعيين: فإن قيل: هذا يجوز في اللون، فإن له وجوداً مضافاً إلى الماهية، زائداً على الماهية؛ ولا يجوز في واجب الوجود، إذ ليس له إلا وجوب الوجود، وليس ثمت ماهية يضاف الوجود إليها؛ وكما أن فصل السواد وفصل الحمرة، لا يشترط تلونية في كونها لونية، إنما يشترط في وجودها الحاصل بعلة، فكذلك ينبغى ألا يشترط في الوجود الواجب، فإن الوجود الواجب للأول كاللونية للون، لا كالوجود المضاف إلى اللونية.
قلنا: لا نسلم، بل إن له حقيقة موصوفة بالوجود، على ما سنبينه في المسألة التي بعد هذه، وقولهم: إنه وجود بلا ماهية خارج عن المعقول. ورجع حاصل الكلام إلى أنهم بنوا نفى التثنية على نفي التركيب الجنسي والفصلى، ثم بنوا ذلك على نفى الماهية وراء الوجود، فمهما أبطلنا الأخير، الذي هو أساس الأساس، بطل الكل عليهم، وهو بنيان ضعيف الثبوت، قريب من بيوت العنكبوت.
From what aspect is this impossible in causes? And by this their inability to deny two makers becomes clear. For it is said: This is only impossible because that by which there is distinction between the two essences, if it is a condition for the necessity of existence, then it should be found in every necessary existent, so they would not be distinct. And if this is not a condition, nor the other a condition, then everything that is not a condition for the necessity of existence, its existence is dispensable, and the necessity of existence is completed by something else. We said: This is exactly what you mentioned concerning the attributes, and we have spoken about it. The source of the confusion is in the term 'necessarily existent (wajib al-wujud)', so let it be discarded. For we do not concede that the proof indicates 'necessarily existent' if 'eternal existent with no agent' is not intended. If this is intended, then let 'necessarily existent' be left aside, and let it be shown that an existent with no cause and no agent, multiplicity and distinction are impossible in it, and no proof establishes it. So their statement remains: Is that [the distinguishing factor] a condition for 'that it have no cause'? It is nonsense. For that which has no cause, we have shown that its having no cause is not caused, so that its condition might be sought. It is like one saying: Is blackness a condition for color being color? If it were a condition, why is redness a color? So it is said: As for its essence (i.e., color-ness), neither of the two is a condition – I mean the subsistence of the reality of color-ness in the mind – and as for its existence (outside the mind), the condition is one of them not specifically determined – i.e., no genus can exist except with a differentia. Likewise, one who posits two causes and terminates the regress by them says: They are distinguished by differentiae, and one of the differentiae is a condition for existence necessarily, but not specifically determined. If it is said: This is permissible for color, for it has an existence added to the quiddity, additional to the quiddity; but it is not permissible for the necessarily existent, for it has only the necessity of existence, and there is no quiddity to which existence is added. And just as the differentia of blackness and the differentia of redness are not a condition for color-ness in its being color-ness, rather they are a condition for its existence that comes about by a cause, so likewise it should not be a condition for the necessary existence, for the necessary existence of the First is like color-ness for color, not like existence added to color-ness. We said: We do not concede. Rather, it has a reality qualified by existence, as we will clarify in the following question. And their statement that it is existence without quiddity is beyond the intelligible. The gist of the matter is that they built the denial of duality on the denial of generic and specific composition, and then built that on the denial of quiddity beyond existence. So once we invalidate the last, which is the foundation of foundations, everything becomes invalid for them, and it is a weak structure, near to spiders' webs.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument. Ghazali responds to the philosophers' claim that two gods are impossible because their distinguishing factor would either be a condition for necessary existence (leading to identical conditions) or not (making it dispensable). Ghazali first points out that the confusion stems from the term 'necessary existent' (wajib al-wujud); he suggests replacing it with 'existent with no cause' to avoid ambiguity. He then argues that the philosophers' question about whether the distinguishing factor is a condition for having no cause is nonsense, because having no cause is not caused and thus requires no condition. He illustrates this with the analogy of blackness and redness: neither is a condition for the essence of color-ness, but for existence, one of them is a condition (but not specifically determined). The philosophers object that this analogy fails because color has an existence added to quiddity, while the necessary existent has only its necessity. Ghazali responds by affirming that the First has a reality qualified by existence, promising to prove this later, and he dismisses the notion of existence without quiddity as unintelligible. He concludes that the philosophers' entire argument against duality rests on shaky foundations (denial of quiddity beyond existence), and once that is refuted, their case collapses like a spider's web.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the necessary existent has no quiddity, making it unique and indivisible.
Correction: Ghazali argues that this notion is unintelligible; the First has a reality qualified by existence. The denial of quiddity is the weak link in the philosophers' argument.

Key Takeaway

The Second Approach: Ilzam Against the Philosophers
Ghazali uses the philosophers' own premises to force the conclusion of multiplicity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali turns the philosophers' own definition of the First as an 'abstract intellect' into a dilemma that forces multiplicity or composition upon the First.

Core Idea
The philosophers' claim that the First has no genus is undone by their own term 'abstract intellect'.

In this passage, Ghazali deploys a powerful rhetorical strategy: he takes the philosophers' own definitions and shows they lead to an unintended conclusion. By accepting that the First is an 'abstract intellect' (aql mujarrad), the philosophers must either accept a duality without distinction or introduce composition through a differentiating factor. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ghazali uses a very tight logical structure.
2
Identify the shared property
Find where Ghazali states that both the First and the other intellects are 'abstract intellects'. This is the key shared property.
3
Understand the dilemma
Ghazali presents two options: either there is no distinction between the First and other intellects, which is absurd; or there is a distinction, which implies composition. Work through both horns.
This is the core of the ilzam argument.
4
Reflect on the refutation
Ask yourself: how does this dilemma refute the philosophers' claim that the First has no genus? The commentary will help you see the connection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسلك الثانى : الإلزام وهو أنا نقول : إن لم يكن الوجود والجوهرية والمبدئية جنساً، لأنه ليس مقولا في جواب ما هو، فالأول عندكم عقل مجرد، كما أن سائر العقول – التي هي المبادئ للوجود، المسماة بالملائكة عندهم، التي هي معلولات الأول - عقول مجردة عن المادة، فهذه الحقيقة تشمل الأول ومعلوله الأول، فإن المعلول الأول أيضاً بسيط لا تركيب في ذاته، إلا من حيث لزومه، وهما مشتركان في أن كل واحد منهما عقل مجرد عن المادة، وهذه حقيقة جنسية، فليست العقلية المجردة للذات من اللوازم، بل هي الماهية، وهذه الماهية مشتركة بين الأول وسائر العقول، فإن لم يباينها بشيء آخر فقد عقلتم اثنينية من غير مباينة، وإن باينها، فما به المباينة غير ما به المشاركة.
The second approach: the ilzam (compelling argument), which is that we say: If existence, substance-ness, and principality are not a genus, because they are not predicated in answer to 'what is it?', then the First for you is an intellect abstract (from matter), just as the other intellects – which are the principles of existence, called angels by them, and which are effects of the First – are intellects abstracted from matter. This reality encompasses the First and its first effect, for the first effect is also simple with no composition in its essence, except in terms of its concomitance. They share in that each of them is an intellect abstract from matter, and this is a generic reality. So abstract intellectuality is not a concomitant of the essence, but rather it is the quiddity. This quiddity is shared between the First and the other intellects. So if it is not distinguished by something else, then you have understood a duality without distinction. And if it is distinguished, then that by which it is distinguished is other than that by which it shares.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents Ghazali's second argument (ilzam, a compelling argument) against the philosophers. He begins by noting that if the philosophers deny that existence, substance-ness, and principality are genera (because they are not predicated in answer to 'what is it?'), then they must admit that the First is an abstract intellect (aql mujarrad). Similarly, the other intellects (the celestial principles they call angels), which are effects of the First, are also abstract intellects. This common property (abstract intellectuality) is a generic reality that encompasses both the First and its first effect. Since both are simple (without composition) and share this quiddity, abstract intellectuality is not merely a concomitant but the very quiddity of these beings. Therefore, either they are distinguished by something else (in which case the distinguishing factor is different from the shared factor, implying composition) or they are not distinguished (in which case we have two identical things without distinction, which is problematic). Either way, the philosophers' own premises lead to a contradiction or to the acceptance of multiplicity and composition in the First.

Correction: The philosophers' own premise that the First is an abstract intellect forces it into a genus shared with other intellects.

Key Takeaway

Refutation of the Philosophers' Claim that the First Has No Essence: The Demand for Proof
Ghazali refutes the philosophers' demand for proof that the First has no essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that the philosophers' claim that God has no essence is not rationally necessary, and that a quiddity does not entail that existence is caused by an efficient cause.

Core Idea
Having an essence does not mean God is caused; the philosophers confuse logical priority with causal dependence.

In this passage, Ghazali takes on the philosophical doctrine that God is simple existence without any quiddity or essence. He first demands a proof for this claim, then systematically dismantles the philosophers' argument that if God had an essence, His existence would be an effect. By distinguishing between different senses of 'dependent' and 'cause', Ghazali shows that the only impossibility is an infinite regress of causes, not the affirmation of a divine essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the flow: Ghazali states the claim, challenges for proof, and then responds to objections.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the philosophers' main argument
The philosophers argue that if God had a quiddity, then existence would be dependent on it, and thus caused. Identify this step in the text.
3
Follow Ghazali's response
Ghazali responds by clarifying the term 'dependent'. He distinguishes between efficient causation and logical priority. Note how he reframes the issue.
Key phrase: 'If they mean by dependent something else, it is conceded.'
4
Understand the conclusion
Ghazali concludes that the philosophers' proof reduces to the proof for negating attributes, but is even weaker. He asserts that a single existent quiddity is conceivable.
The error is thinking that quiddity and existence constitute multiplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي مسألة [٨] في إبطال قولهم : إن وجود الأول بسيط هو وجود محض ، ولا ماهية ولا حقيقة يضاف الوجود إليها بل الوجود الواجب له كالماهية لغيره والكلام عليه من وجهين : الأول المطالبة بالدليل : فيقال : بم عرفتم ذلك ؟ ! أبضرورة العقل أو نظره ؟! وليس بضروری، فلابد من ذكر طريق النظر . فإن قيل: لأنه لو كانت له ماهية ، لكان الوجود مضافاً إليها ، وتابعاً لها ، ولازماً لها ، والتابع معلول ، فيكون الوجود الواجب معلولا ، وهو متناقض . فنقول : هذا رجوع إلى منبع التلبيس ، في إطلاق لفظ الوجود الواجب ، فإنا نقول : له حقيقة وماهية ، وتلك الحقيقة موجودة – أي ليست معدومة منفية - ووجودها مضاف إليها ، وإن أحبوا أن يسموه تابعاً ولازماً ، فلا مشاحة في الأسامى، بعد أن يعرف أنه لا فاعل للوجود ، بل لم يزل هذا الوجود قديماً ، من غير علة فاعلية . فإن عنوا بالتابع والمعلول ، أن له علة فاعلية ، فليس كذلك ، وإن عنوا غيره فهو مسلم ولا استحالة فيه ، إذ الدليل لم يدل إلا على قطع تسلسل العلل ، وقطعه بحقيقة موجودة ، وماهية ثابتة ، ممكن" ؛ فليس يحتاج فيه إلى سلب الماهية فإن قيل : فتكون الماهية سبباً للوجود الذى هو تابع لها ، فيكون الوجود معلولا ومفعولا قلنا : الماهية في الأشياء الحادثة لا تكون سبباً للوجود ، فكيف في القديم إن عنوا بالسبب الفاعل له ؛ وإن عنوا به وجهاً آخر ، - وهو أنه لا يستغنى عنه - فليكن كذلك ، ولا استحالة فيه ، إنما الاستحالة في تسلسل العلل ، فإذا انقطع ، فقد اندفعت الاستحالة ، وما عدا ذلك لم تعرف استحالته ، فلابد من برهان على استحالته ، وكل براهينهم تحكمات ، مبناها على أخذ لفظ « واجب الوجود» بمعنى له لوازم ، وتسلم (1) أن الدليل قد دل على واجب وجود بالنعت الذى وصفوه ، وليس كذلك كما سبق . وعلى الجملة ، دليلهم في هذا يرجع إلى دليل نفي الصفات ، ونفى الانقسام الجنسى والفصلى ، إلا أنه أغمض وأضعف ؛ لأن هذه الكثرة لا ترجع إلا إلى مجرد اللفظ ، وإلا فالعقل يتسع لتقدير ماهية واحدة موجودة ؛ وهم يقولون : كل ماهية موجودة فمتكثرة ، إذ فيه ما هية ووجود ، وهذا غاية الضلال ، فإن الموجود الواحد معقول بكل حال ، ولا موجود إلا وله حقيقة ، ووجود الحقيقة لا ينفى الوحدة .
Question [8]: On invalidating their statement that the existence of the First is simple, pure existence, with no quiddity (māhiyya) or reality (ḥaqīqa) to which existence is attributed; rather, Necessary Existence (al-wujūb al-wājib) has existence as what quiddity is for others. The discussion on it is from two aspects: The first aspect: the demand for proof. So it is said: By what did you know that? Is it by rational necessity or by its consideration? It is not necessary, so it is obligatory to mention a way of consideration. For if it is said: Because if He had a quiddity, then existence would be attributed to it, dependent on it, and necessary for it, and the dependent is an effect (ma‘lūl), so Necessary Existence would be an effect, which is contradictory. We say: This is a return to the source of obfuscation in the use of the term 'Necessary Existence'. For we say: He has a reality and quiddity, and that reality is existent—i.e., not non-existent nor negated—and its existence is attributed to it. And if they wish to call it 'dependent' and 'necessary', there is no dispute over names, after it is known that there is no agent (fā‘il) for existence; rather, this existence has always been eternal without an efficient cause. If they mean by 'dependent' and 'effect' that it has an efficient cause, then that is not the case; if they mean something else, it is conceded and there is no impossibility in it. For the proof only indicated the termination of the chain of causes (tasalsul al-‘ilal), and its termination at an existing reality and a fixed quiddity, a possible (mumkin) one; so there is no need to negate quiddity. Then if it is said: Then the quiddity would be a cause (sabab) for the existence that is dependent on it, so existence would be an effect and made. We say: Quiddity in contingent things is not a cause for existence, so how about the Eternal? If they mean by 'cause' the efficient cause; or if they mean another aspect—namely that it is not independent of it—then let it be so, and there is no impossibility in it. Impossibility is only in the chain of causes; when it is terminated, the impossibility is removed. Beyond that, its impossibility is not known, so a proof for its impossibility is necessary. All their proofs are arbitrary judgments, based on taking the term 'Necessary Existence' to mean having necessary concomitants (lawāzim), and they claim that the proof has indicated a necessary existent with the description they described, but it is not so, as previously. In summary, their proof in this matter reduces to the proof of the negation of attributes (nafy al-ṣifāt) and the negation of generic and specific differentiation, except that it is more obscure and weaker; because this multiplicity reduces only to mere wording. Otherwise, the mind can conceive of a single quiddity that is existent. They say: Every existent quiddity is multiple, because it has quiddity and existence. This is extreme error, for the one existent is intelligible in every case, and there is no existent except that it has a reality, and the existence of the reality does not negate unity.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the philosophers' claim that the First (God) is pure existence without any essence or quiddity. Ghazali begins by stating the question and then introduces two aspects of discussion. The first aspect is the demand for proof. He challenges the philosophers to explain how they know this: is it by rational intuition or by reasoning? Since it is not obvious, they must provide a rational argument. They respond with an objection: if the First had a quiddity (māhiyya), then existence would be attributed to it, dependent on it, and necessary for it. The dependent (tābi‘) would then be an effect (ma‘lūl), making Necessary Existence an effect, which is contradictory. Ghazali responds by calling this a return to obfuscation regarding the term 'Necessary Existence'. He asserts that God has both reality (ḥaqīqa) and quiddity, but His reality is existent—not non-existent—and existence is attributed to it. If the philosophers call this 'dependent', there is no quarrel over terminology as long as it is clear that there is no efficient cause for existence; the existence is eternal without an efficient cause. Ghazali clarifies that if by 'dependent' and 'effect' they mean an efficient cause, that is denied; if they mean something else (like logical priority), it is conceded and not impossible. The proof only shows that the chain of causes must end at an existing reality and a fixed quiddity—a possible (mumkin) being—so there is no need to negate quiddity. 

The philosophers then raise a second objection: if quiddity is a cause (sabab) for existence, then existence would be an effect and 'made' (maf‘ūl). Ghazali counters that in contingent things, quiddity is not a cause for existence, so how could it be so for the Eternal? If they mean the efficient cause, it is false; if they mean another aspect—such as dependence—then it is unobjectionable. Impossibility only lies in an infinite regress of causes; once the chain is cut, impossibility is removed. No further impossibility is proven; the burden is on them to provide a proof. Their proofs are arbitrary, based on understanding 'Necessary Existence' as having necessary concomitants, but the proof does not necessitate their description. 

Ghazali concludes that their argument reduces to the argument for negating attributes (nafy al-ṣifāt) and negating generic and specific differentiation, but it is even more obscure and weaker. Their alleged multiplicity (of quiddity and existence) is merely verbal; the mind can conceive of a single existent quiddity. Their claim that every existent quiddity is multiple because it has quiddity and existence is extreme error, because a single existent is intelligible, and every existent has a reality, and the existence of that reality does not negate unity.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God has an essence, then His existence would be an effect of that essence, and thus He would be caused.
Correction: Ghazali shows that the dependency meant by the philosophers could be logical or ontological priority, not efficient causation. The only real impossibility is an infinite regress of causes, not the mere possession of an essence.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali refutes the philosophers by showing that affirming a divine essence does not imply causation; the only impossibility is an infinite regress of causes.

The Second Approach: Existence without Essence is Unintelligible
Ghazali argues that existence without essence is inconceivable and leads to contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali argues that existence without quiddity (essence) is unintelligible and how this refutes the philosophers' claim about the First.

Core Idea
Existence without essence is a contradiction in terms.

Ghazali presents his second argument against the philosophers' view that the First is pure existence without quiddity. He will show that such a concept is not only meaningless but leads to contradictions when applied to contingent beings. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without analyzing. Notice how Ghazali uses an analogy with absolute non-existence to frame his argument.
The passage begins with a strong claim: 'Existence without quiddity is unintelligible.'
2
Analyze the reductio argument
Find the evidence section beginning with 'Evidence for this is...' Understand how Ghazali uses the impossibility of existence without essence in effects to prove the concept's incoherence.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum: if the concept were coherent, it would apply to contingent beings, but it does not.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider Ghazali's final remark: 'The end of reaching such a level in intelligibles is the depth of their darkness.' What does he mean by this?
The passage breaks off, but the intent is clear: the philosophers' concept is fundamentally flawed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسلك الثانى : هو أن نقول : وجود بلا ماهية ولا حقيقة ، غير معقول ، وكما لا نعقل عدماً مرسلاً ، إلا بالإضافة إلى موجود يقدر عدمه ، فلا نعقل وجوداً مرسلاً ، إلا بالإضافة إلى حقيقة معينة، لا سيما إذا تعين ذاتاً واحدة ، فكيف يتعين واحداً متميزاً عن غيره بالمعنى ، ولا حقيقة له ؟ ! فإن نفى الماهية نفى للحقيقة ، وإذا انتفت حقيقة الموجود ، لم يعقل الوجود ؛ فكأنهم قالوا : وجود لا موجود ، وهو متناقض . ويدل عليه أنه لو كان هذا معقولا ، لجاز أن يكون في المعلولات وجود لا حقيقة له ، يشارك الأول فى كونه وجوداً لا حقيقة له ولا ماهية له ، ويباينه في أن له علة ، والأول لا علة له ، فلم لا يتصور هذا في المعلولات ؟! وهل له سبب إلا أنه غير معقول في نفسه ؟! وما لا يعقل في نفسه ، فبأن تنفى علته لا يصير معقولا ! وما يعقل ، فبأن تقدر له علة لا يخرج عن كونه معقولا والتناهى إلى هذا الحد في المعقولات ، غاية ظلماتهم ، فقد ظنوا أنهم
The second approach: that we say: Existence without quiddity (māhiyya) and without reality (ḥaqīqa) is unintelligible (ghayr ma‘qūl). Just as we do not conceive of absolute non-existence (ʿadaman mursalan) except in relation to an existent whose non-existence is estimated, so we do not conceive of absolute existence (wujūdan mursalan) except in relation to a specific reality, especially if it is determined as a single essence. So how can it be determined as one distinguished from others in meaning, while having no reality? For negation of quiddity is negation of reality, and when the reality of the existent is negated, existence is not intelligible. So it is as if they said: an existence without an existent, which is contradictory. Evidence for this is: if this were intelligible, then it would be possible that among effects there be an existence without reality, sharing with the First in being an existence without reality and without quiddity, but differing in that it has a cause while the First has no cause. So why is this not conceived in effects? Is there any reason except that it is unintelligible in itself? What is unintelligible in itself does not become intelligible by negating its cause. And what is intelligible, if a cause is posited for it, does not cease to be intelligible. The end of reaching such a level in intelligibles is the depth of their darkness; they thought that they...
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage contains Ghazali's second approach (al-maslak al-thānī) in refuting the philosophers' claim that the First is pure existence without quiddity. He begins by asserting that existence without quiddity or reality is unintelligible. He draws an analogy: just as we cannot conceive of absolute non-existence except in relation to an existent whose non-existence is supposed, similarly we cannot conceive of absolute existence except in relation to a specific reality. This is especially true if this existence is determined as a single, distinct essence. How can something be a single essence, distinguished from others by its meaning, if it has no reality? Negating quiddity is negating reality, and if the reality of the existent is negated, then existence itself becomes unintelligible. This leads to a contradiction: an existence without an existent.

Ghazali then provides evidence (wa yadullu ʿalayhi): if such a thing were intelligible, then it should be possible for contingent effects (maʿlūlāt) to have existence without reality—sharing with the First the property of being existence without reality or quiddity, but differing in that they have a cause while the First has no cause. But this is not conceived in effects. The only reason is that such a thing is unintelligible in itself. Something unintelligible in itself does not become intelligible by removing its cause; likewise, something intelligible does not become unintelligible by positing a cause. Ghazali concludes that reaching this level in intelligibles is the depth of the philosophers' darkness; they thought that they... (the text breaks off). The argument is a reductio: if the philosophers' concept of pure existence were coherent, it would apply to contingent beings as well, but it does not, proving its incoherence.

Key Terms
وجود مرسل
عدم مرسل
ماهية
حقيقة
معقول
معلول
علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that an abstract concept like 'existence' can be meaningful without any reference to a specific reality.
Correction: Ghazali shows that existence must always be tied to a quiddity (essence); otherwise, it is unintelligible and contradictory.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali's second approach, why is 'existence without quiddity' unintelligible?
A) Because it would require a cause, but the First has no cause.
B) Because we cannot conceive of absolute non-existence without an existent, similarly we cannot conceive of absolute existence without a specific reality.
C) Because it leads to an infinite regress of causes.
D) Because quiddity is the same as existence in the First.

Key Takeaway
Existence must be attached to a quiddity; otherwise it is unintelligible and contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever thought of God as an abstract 'existence' or a general 'force' without a concrete reality? How does Ghazali's argument challenge you to know His actual attributes?
?
If existence without quiddity is meaningless, then every real thing has a specific nature. What does this say about the way you approach knowing Allah through His names and attributes? Does your worship reflect a personal connection with a defined Reality or a vague concept?
?
Consider an area of your life where you treat your own existence as 'just there' without purpose. How does Ghazali's insistence that existence must be tied to a reality push you to seek the purpose (quiddity) of your own being?

Ghazali's Critique of the Philosophers' Proof
Ghazali critiques the philosophers' proof and reduces it to a weaker argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's critique that the philosophers' proof for the Necessary Existent is arbitrary and reduces to a weaker argument about negating attributes and division.

Core Idea
The philosophers' proof for the Necessary Existent is weaker than they claim.

Ghazali challenges the philosophers' argument for a Necessary Existent, asserting that their proof is not substantive but built on a misunderstanding. He argues that the only recognized impossibility is an infinite regress of causes, and once that is cut off, no impossibility remains. The philosophers' proofs are arbitrary and ultimately reduce to a weaker form. Let's examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Get the overall gist of Ghazali's critique.
Pay attention to his dismissive tone towards the philosophers' proofs.
2
Identify his point about impossibility
Ghazali states that the only known impossibility is an infinite chain of causes. Once it is cut off, there is no impossibility. For anything else, a proof of impossibility is required.
He is not rejecting the concept of impossibility, only the philosophers' application.
3
Examine his critique of philosophers' proofs
He calls their proofs 'arbitrary' (تحكمات), based on taking 'necessary existent' as having necessary concomitants, and assuming their description is proven – which it is not.
Earlier he had argued that the term 'necessary existent' does not imply the attributes they assign.
4
Understand the reduction
Ghazali concludes that their entire proof reduces to the proof for negating attributes and negating generic and specific division, and he says this version is even more obscure and weaker.
This connects to earlier discussions on divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنه - فليكن كذلك ، ولا استحالة فيه ، إنما الاستحالة في تسلسل العلل ، فإذا انقطع ، فقد اندفعت الاستحالة ، وما عدا ذلك لم تعرف استحالته ، فلابد من برهان على استحالته ، وكل براهينهم تحكمات ، مبناها على أخذ لفظ « واجب الوجود» بمعنى له لوازم ، وتسلم أن الدليل قد دل على واجب وجود ) بالنعت الذى وصفوه ، وليس كذلك كما سبق . وعلى الجملة ، دليلهم في هذا يرجع إلى دليل نفي الصفات ، ونفى الانقسام الجنسى والفصلى ، إلا أنه أغمض وأضعف .
From it - so let it be thus, and there is no impossibility in it; impossibility only lies in the chain of causes. When it is cut off, the impossibility is removed. Apart from that, its impossibility is not known, so a proof of its impossibility is necessary. All of their proofs are arbitrary, based on taking the term 'necessary existent' (wājib al-wujūd) in the sense of having necessary concomitants, and they assume that proof has indicated a necessary existent with the attribute they described, but it is not so as previously mentioned. In summary, their proof in this matter reduces to the proof of negating attributes, and negating generic and specific division, except that it is more obscure and weaker.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the philosophers' proof for a necessary existent. Ghazali begins by discussing the impossibility of an infinite regress of causes. He states that the only recognized impossibility is the chain of causes; once it is cut off, the impossibility is removed. For anything else, we need a proof of its impossibility. He then asserts that all the philosophers' proofs are arbitrary, built upon taking the term 'necessary existent' to mean something that has necessary concomitants, and assuming that proof has demonstrated such a being with the specific attribute they describe—but this is not established, as already mentioned. Finally, Ghazali summarizes that their proof ultimately reduces to the proof for negating attributes and negating generic and specific division, but this version is even more obscure and weaker than that.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود (wājib al-wujūd)
نفي الصفات (nafy al-ṣifāt)
الانقسام الجنسى والفصلى (al-inqisām al-jinsī wa al-faṣlī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ghazali fully rejects the impossibility of infinite regress.
Correction: He only rejects the philosophers' specific application, not the concept itself. He acknowledges impossibility only in the chain of causes.

Checkpoint
To what does Ghazali say the philosophers' proof ultimately reduce?
A) A proof of the existence of attributes
B) A proof of the necessity of division
C) The proof for negating attributes and negating generic and specific division
D) A proof of the contingency of the world

Key Takeaway
Ghazali argues that the philosophers' proof for the Necessary Existent ultimately reduces to a weaker argument about negating attributes and division.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own belief in Allah, do you find yourself relying on complex intellectual arguments that might be weaker than you think? How does Ghazali's critique challenge you to seek a firmer foundation for your faith—not just rational proofs, but direct engagement with revelation and inner certainty?
?
Ghazali says the philosophers' proofs are 'arbitrary' because they assume a specific meaning for 'Necessary Existent.' Are there aspects of your understanding of Allah that are really based on assumptions you haven't examined—assumptions inherited from culture or personal preference? What would it mean to honestly scrutinize those assumptions and let them go if they don't align with the Qur'an and Sunnah?
?
This passage shows that even sophisticated scholarly arguments can be obscure and weak. In your daily life, how often do you rely on superficial reasoning about Allah—just enough to feel satisfied? Commit today to studying the Qur'an and the Prophet's ﷺ teachings directly, with the intention to strengthen your conviction and sincerity, rather than merely defending a position.
